[Update: I have now used it a couple of more times and realized there's a way to change modes without making a mess or having it on high power inside my mouth. I wet and put toothpaste on the head b4 placing it on the brush, then turn on the brush clicking the mode button until the &#34;feather&#34; lights up, then turn the brush off and place the already prepared brush head back onto the powered part. Now it's ready to go and already on sensitive setting. (The brush keeps the &#34;mode&#34; for 20-30 seconds while not turned on.) I have also started using it on sensitive for 3 of the 30 second intervals, then switch it to polish for the last 30 second interval. Instead of doing the &#34;quadrants,&#34; I brush the biting surfaces for 30 seconds, the back of my teeth for 30 seconds, and then the front for 30 seconds; so the last 30 seconds on polish I go over all the teeth for a sweep or two. It seems to keep my teeth from being painful, yet does a more thorough job.]

This just felt like a cheap disposable electronic brush that I spent 10x too much for. It's louder which adds to the whole mechanical feel as it gyrates in your mouth. Because I already used the product I couldn't return to Amazon but I contacted Oral-B directly. Luckily, they offer a 60-day challenge and guarantee a full refund for unsatisfied users. I FedEx'd the toothbrush back and have to wait 8-10 weeks for my refund. If you're interested in doing the same you can call their Customer Service line (800-566-7252) for more information. The shipping address that was provided to me was as follows: Attn: 60 Day Challenge Oral-B Braun Division The Procter & Gamble Company Sobin Park and A Street, MS 1F South Boston, MA 02127 Wished I could say I didn't have to go through all the trouble of returning but hopefully this info. helps those of you looking to return your used product.

This means that it suffers from a memory effect and really only lasts 10 days for just one person. I minimize the memory effect by fully charging it when it is mostly discharged, rather than storing the handle in the charger every night. I have been using this product for about 2 months and I am very happy with it, but I only rated it with 4 stars due to the cons described below. I have been an Oral B customer for many years. I purchased the product to replace my very reliable Oral B Ultra which lasted a good 6 or 7 years. I selected the 4000 model based on other reviews and I am happy to confirm that I agree with them, particularly the comments on the 5000 model vs. the 4000. There is no need for the wireless gadget. The product has a built in timer which briefly stops the brush head every 30 seconds so that you know when to move to the next quadrant in your mouth. Save the extra cost and use it to buy additional brush heads. I like many of the design changes implemented since my last model, but I do not care for the requirement to change the brush mode after the unit is started. It is hard to see the icon light up when you have the brush head in your mouth, so you have to guess what mode you selected while the timer is running. It would have been much better if they allowed you to select the brush mode before starting the unit. I am also disappointed with the charging base. It takes almost 24 hours to fully recharge the unit. My previous product only took a few hours. In addition, and just like others reported, I cannot get 10 days of use before recharging. I am getting 5 days at best. The charger base is oval shaped and therefore not compatible with previous versions. It also only works with 110 volts. This creates a problem for me since I often travel to other countries and therefore cannot charge the unit while I am traveling. The old chargersworked with any voltage between 110V and 240V, so you could plug them anywhere in the world by simply carrying a plug adapter. Other than that, you will likely be happy until you need to buy new brush heads (the unit comes with one). They are terribly expensive!
